       <article class="content-wrapper wrapper clearfix detail-block-md" id="article-26226">
        <header class="content-header">
         <h1>
          What Man Thinks Is Recycling Takes City Workers 2 Hours A Day To Sort
         </h1>
        </header>
        <main class="content-body large-thing" data-area="Article Body">
         <div class="content-masthead">
         </div>
         <div class="content-meta small-thing">
          <div>
           <a class="content-type" data-track-action="Meta: Feature Type" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/search?tags=" href="/features/news-in-brief">
            NEWS IN BRIEF
           </a>
           <span class="content-published">
            October 1, 2011
           </span>
          </div>
          <div>
           <span class="content-issue">
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Issue" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/issue/4740/" href="/issue/4740/">
             Vol 47 Issue 40
            </a>
            <span class="bul">
             
            </span>
           </span>
           <span class="content-tags">
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Tags" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/tag/local" href="/tag/local">
             Local
            </a>
            <span class="bul">
             
            </span>
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Tags" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/tag/environment" href="/tag/environment">
             Environment
            </a>
           </span>
          </div>
          <div class="article-share-tools share-container">
           <div class="share-tools share-widget" data-share-description="NEW YORKCity sanitation experts confirmed yesterday that the supposed recycling of Manhattan resident Ron Klauff was in fact a conglomeration of various recyclable and nonrecyclable refuse that takes city workers an average of two hours and 288 gallons of water to sort and clean each week." data-share-image="http://i.onionstatic.com/onion/None/16x9/1200.jpg" data-share-redirect-url="http://www.theonion.com/fb-close" data-share-title="What Man Thinks Is Recycling Takes City Workers 2 Hours A Day To Sort" data-share-url="http://www.theonion.com/r/26226">
            <a class="share-facebook button" data-action="Facebook share clicked" data-track-action="Meta: Share" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="Facebook" href="#" target="_blank" title="Share via Facebook">
             <i class="fa fa-facebook fa-fw">
             </i>
            </a>
            <a class="share-twitter button" data-action="Twitter share clicked" data-track-action="Meta: Share" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="Twitter" href="#" title="Share via Twitter">
             <i class="fa fa-twitter fa-fw">
             </i>
            </a>
            <a class="share-mail button" data-action="Email share clicked" data-track-action="Meta: Share" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="Email" href="#" title="Share via Email">
             <i class="fa fa-envelope fa-fw">
             </i>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="dfp dfp-slot-article-button" data-ad-unit="article-button" data-targeting='{"dfp_pagetype": "article", "dfp_content_id": 26226}'>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="large-thing content-main">
          <div class="content-text">
           <div>
            <p>
             NEW YORKCity sanitation experts confirmed yesterday that the supposed recycling of Manhattan resident Ron Klauff was in fact a conglomeration of various recyclable and nonrecyclable refuse that takes city workers an average of two hours and 288 gallons of water to sort and clean each week. These days, being eco-aware is more important than ever, said Klauff, filling a plastic shopping bag with a mixture of yogurt containers, wire hangers, and broken electronics that a civil servant will later have to sift through in the middle of the night. You have to do your part, even if that means gathering all of your soda cans and stacking them neatly inside your pizza boxes. Because Klauff is the only New York resident who does not carefully sort and separate his recyclables, officials are considering just tossing everything he throws out into a landfill.
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
